</p>
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Intense armed conflict</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">This article is about war in general. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/War_(disambiguation)" title="War (disambiguation)">War (disambiguation)</a>, <a class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" href="/wiki/The_War_(disambiguation)" title="The War (disambiguation)">The War (disambiguation)</a>, and <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Warring_(disambiguation)" title="Warring (disambiguation)">Warring (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

For the metal band, see <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Warfare_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Warfare (band) (page does not exist)">Warfare (band)</a>.</div>

</tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1063604349">.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar ul{display:inline-block;white-space:nowrap;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::before{margin-right:-0.125em;content:"[ "}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::after{margin-left:-0.125em;content:" ]"}.mw-parser-output .navbar li{word-spacing:-0.125em}.mw-parser-output .navbar a>span,.mw-parser-output .navbar a>abbr{text-decoration:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-mini abbr{font-variant:small-caps;border-bottom:none;text-decoration:none;cursor:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-full{font-size:114%;margin:0 7em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-mini{font-size:114%;margin:0 4em}</style><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:War" title="Template:War"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:War" title="Template talk:War"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:War&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>War</b> is an intense <b>armed conflict</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[a]</a></sup> between <a href="/wiki/State_(polity)" title="State (polity)">states</a>, <a href="/wiki/Government" title="Government">governments</a>, <a href="/wiki/Society" title="Society">societies</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Paramilitary" title="Paramilitary">paramilitary</a> groups such as <a href="/wiki/Mercenary" title="Mercenary">mercenaries</a>, <a href="/wiki/Insurgency" title="Insurgency">insurgents</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Militia" title="Militia">militias</a>. It is generally characterized by extreme <a href="/wiki/Violence" title="Violence">violence</a>, destruction, and mortality, using <a href="/wiki/Regular_army" title="Regular army">regular</a> or <a href="/wiki/Irregular_military" title="Irregular military">irregular</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_forces" title="Military forces">military forces</a>. <b>Warfare</b> refers to the common activities and characteristics of types of war, or of wars in general.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[2]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Total_war" title="Total war">Total war</a> is warfare that is not restricted to purely <a href="/wiki/Legitimate_military_target" title="Legitimate military target">legitimate military targets</a>, and can result in massive <a href="/wiki/Civilian_casualties" title="Civilian casualties">civilian</a> or other <a href="/wiki/Non-combatant" title="Non-combatant">non-combatant</a> suffering and <a href="/wiki/Casualty_(person)" title="Casualty (person)">casualties</a>.
</p><p>While some <a href="/wiki/War_studies" title="War studies">war studies</a> scholars consider war a universal and ancestral aspect of <a href="/wiki/Human_nature" title="Human nature">human nature</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[3]</a></sup> others argue it is a result of specific socio-cultural, economic or ecological circumstances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sage_Publications_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sage_Publications-5">[4]</a></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886046785">.mw-parser-output .toclimit-2 .toclevel-1 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-3 .toclevel-2 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-4 .toclevel-3 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-5 .toclevel-4 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-6 .toclevel-5 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-7 .toclevel-6 ul{display:none}</style><div class="toclimit-3"><div aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading" class="toc" id="toc" role="navigation"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-7"><a href="#Effects"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Effects</span></a>
<ul>
<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-8"><a href="#Military_and_civilian_casualties_in_recent_human_history"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">Military and civilian casualties in recent human history</span></a></li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gari-Melchers-War-Highsmith.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1865" data-file-width="5436" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Gari-Melchers-War-Highsmith.jpeg/350px-Gari-Melchers-War-Highsmith.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Gari-Melchers-War-Highsmith.jpeg/525px-Gari-Melchers-War-Highsmith.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Gari-Melchers-War-Highsmith.jpeg/700px-Gari-Melchers-War-Highsmith.jpeg 2x" width="350"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gari-Melchers-War-Highsmith.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mural of War (1896), by <a href="/wiki/Gari_Melchers" title="Gari Melchers">Gari Melchers</a></div></div></div>
<p>The English word <i>war</i> derives from the 11th-century <a href="/wiki/Old_English" title="Old English">Old English</a> words <i>wyrre</i> and <i>werre</i>, from <a href="/wiki/Old_French" title="Old French">Old French</a> <i>werre</i> (also <i>guerre</i> as in modern French), in turn from the <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">Frankish</a> *<i>werra</i>, ultimately deriving from the <a href="/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" title="Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a> *<i>werzÅ</i> 'mixture, confusion'. The word is related to the <a href="/wiki/Old_Saxon" title="Old Saxon">Old Saxon</a> <i>werran</i>, <a href="/wiki/Old_High_German" title="Old High German">Old High German</a> <i>werran</i>, and the German <i>verwirren</i>, meaning "to confuse", "to perplex", and "to bring into confusion".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[5]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_history" title="Military history">Military history</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:War_deaths_caused_by_warfare.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="704" data-file-width="1173" decoding="async" height="186" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/War_deaths_caused_by_warfare.svg/310px-War_deaths_caused_by_warfare.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/War_deaths_caused_by_warfare.svg/465px-War_deaths_caused_by_warfare.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/War_deaths_caused_by_warfare.svg/620px-War_deaths_caused_by_warfare.svg.png 2x" width="310"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:War_deaths_caused_by_warfare.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The percentages of men killed in war in eight tribal societies, and Europe and the U.S. in the 20th century. (Lawrence H. Keeley, archeologist)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ramesseum_siege_of_Dapur.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="614" data-file-width="410" decoding="async" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Ramesseum_siege_of_Dapur.jpg/170px-Ramesseum_siege_of_Dapur.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Ramesseum_siege_of_Dapur.jpg/255px-Ramesseum_siege_of_Dapur.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Ramesseum_siege_of_Dapur.jpg/340px-Ramesseum_siege_of_Dapur.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ramesseum_siege_of_Dapur.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Egyptian <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Dapur" title="Siege of Dapur">siege of Dapur</a> in the 13th century BC, from <a href="/wiki/Ramesseum" title="Ramesseum">Ramesseum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thebes,_Egypt" title="Thebes, Egypt">Thebes</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The earliest evidence of <a href="/wiki/Prehistoric_warfare" title="Prehistoric warfare">prehistoric warfare</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Mesolithic" title="Mesolithic">Mesolithic</a> cemetery in <a href="/wiki/Jebel_Sahaba" title="Jebel Sahaba">Jebel Sahaba</a>, which has been determined to be approximately 14,000 years old. About forty-five percent of the skeletons there displayed signs of violent death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Keeley_page_37_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Keeley_page_37-7">[6]</a></sup> Since the rise of the <a href="/wiki/State_(polity)" title="State (polity)">state</a> some 5,000 years ago,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[7]</a></sup> military activity has occurred over much of the globe. The advent of <a href="/wiki/Gunpowder" title="Gunpowder">gunpowder</a> and the acceleration of technological advances led to modern warfare. According to Conway W. Henderson, "One source claims that 14,500 wars have taken place between 3500 BC and the late 20th century, costing 3.5 billion lives, leaving only 300 years of peace (Beer 1981: 20)."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[8]</a></sup> An unfavorable review of this estimate<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[9]</a></sup> mentions the following regarding one of the proponents of this estimate: "In addition, perhaps feeling that the war casualties figure was improbably high, he changed 'approximately 3,640,000,000 human beings have been killed by war or the diseases produced by war' to 'approximately 1,240,000,000 human beings...&amp;c.'" The lower figure is more plausible,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[10]</a></sup> but could still be on the high side considering that the 100 deadliest acts of mass violence between 480 BC and 2002 AD (wars and other man-made disasters with at least 300,000 and up to 66 million victims) claimed about 455 million human lives in total.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[11]</a></sup> Primitive warfare is estimated to have accounted for 15.1% of deaths and claimed 400 million victims.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[12]</a></sup> Added to the aforementioned  figure of 1,240 million between 3500 BC and the late 20th century, this would mean a total of 1,640,000,000 people killed by war (including deaths from famine and disease caused by war) throughout the history and pre-history of mankind. For comparison, an estimated 1,680,000,000 people died from infectious diseases in the 20th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup>
</p><p>In <i><a href="/wiki/War_Before_Civilization" title="War Before Civilization">War Before Civilization</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Lawrence_H._Keeley" title="Lawrence H. Keeley">Lawrence H. Keeley</a>, a professor at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana%E2%80%93Champaign" title="University of Illinois at UrbanaâChampaign">University of Illinois</a>, says approximately 90â95% of known societies throughout history engaged in at least occasional warfare,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[14]</a></sup> and many fought constantly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup>
</p><p>Keeley describes several styles of primitive combat such as small raids, large raids, and massacres. All of these forms of warfare were used by primitive societies, a finding supported by other researchers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup> Keeley explains that early war raids were not well organized, as the participants did not have any formal training. Scarcity of resources meant defensive works were not a cost-effective way to protect the society against enemy raids.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Keeley_page_55_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Keeley_page_55-18">[17]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/William_Rubinstein" title="William Rubinstein">William Rubinstein</a> wrote "Pre-literate societies, even those organised in a relatively advanced way, were renowned for their studied cruelty...'archaeology yields evidence of prehistoric massacres more severe than any recounted in ethnography [i.e., after the coming of the Europeans].'"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MokoShuraiE-Kotoba_IV.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="740" data-file-width="1597" decoding="async" height="111" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/MokoShuraiE-Kotoba_IV.jpg/240px-MokoShuraiE-Kotoba_IV.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/MokoShuraiE-Kotoba_IV.jpg/360px-MokoShuraiE-Kotoba_IV.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/MokoShuraiE-Kotoba_IV.jpg/480px-MokoShuraiE-Kotoba_IV.jpg 2x" width="240"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MokoShuraiE-Kotoba_IV.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Japanese <a href="/wiki/Samurai" title="Samurai">samurai</a> attacking a <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">Mongol</a> ship, 13th century</div></div></div>
<p>In Western Europe, since the late 18th century, more than 150 conflicts and about 600 battles have taken place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-War_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-War-20">[19]</a></sup> During the 20th century, war resulted in a dramatic intensification of the pace of social changes, and was a crucial catalyst for the emergence of the political Left as a force to be reckoned with.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kolko_1994_xviitoxviii_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kolko_1994_xviitoxviii-21">[20]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_War_in_Finland,_1940_HU55566.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3867" data-file-width="5434" decoding="async" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/The_War_in_Finland%2C_1940_HU55566.jpg/220px-The_War_in_Finland%2C_1940_HU55566.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/The_War_in_Finland%2C_1940_HU55566.jpg/330px-The_War_in_Finland%2C_1940_HU55566.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/The_War_in_Finland%2C_1940_HU55566.jpg/440px-The_War_in_Finland%2C_1940_HU55566.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_War_in_Finland,_1940_HU55566.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Finnish soldiers during the <a href="/wiki/Winter_War" title="Winter War">Winter War</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>In 1947, in view of the rapidly increasingly destructive consequences of modern warfare, and with a particular concern for the consequences and costs of the newly developed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atom_bomb" title="Atom bomb">atom bomb</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein" title="Albert Einstein">Albert Einstein</a> famously stated, "I know not with what weapons World War III will be fought, but World War IV will be fought with sticks and stones."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EinsteinWWIV_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-EinsteinWWIV-22">[21]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Mao_Zedong" title="Mao Zedong">Mao Zedong</a> urged the socialist camp not to fear <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nuclear_war" title="Nuclear war">nuclear war</a> with the United States since, even if "half of mankind died, the other half would remain while imperialism would be razed to the ground and the whole world would become socialist."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup>
</p><p>A distinctive feature of war since 1945 is that combat has largely been a matter of civil wars and insurgencies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup> The major exceptions were the <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korean War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Indo-Pakistani_War_of_1971" title="Indo-Pakistani War of 1971">Indo-Pakistani War of 1971</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Iraq_War" title="IranâIraq War">IranâIraq War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_War" title="Gulf War">Gulf War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Eritrean%E2%80%93Ethiopian_War" title="EritreanâEthiopian War">EritreanâEthiopian War</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Ukrainian_War" title="Russo-Ukrainian War">Russo-Ukrainian War</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Abrams_in_formation.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1860" data-file-width="2790" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Abrams_in_formation.jpg/220px-Abrams_in_formation.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Abrams_in_formation.jpg/330px-Abrams_in_formation.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Abrams_in_formation.jpg/440px-Abrams_in_formation.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Abrams_in_formation.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>American tanks moving in formation during the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_War" title="Gulf War">Gulf War</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Human_Security_Report_2005" title="Human Security Report 2005">Human Security Report 2005</a> documented a significant decline in the number and severity of armed conflicts since the end of the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> in the early 1990s. However, the evidence examined in the 2008 edition of the Center for International Development and Conflict Management's "Peace and Conflict" study indicated the overall decline in conflicts had stalled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Types_of_warfare">Types of warfare</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Outline_of_war#Types_of_war" title="Outline of war">Types of war</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Australian_infantry_small_box_respirators_Ypres_1917.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1607" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="228" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Australian_infantry_small_box_respirators_Ypres_1917.jpg/170px-Australian_infantry_small_box_respirators_Ypres_1917.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Australian_infantry_small_box_respirators_Ypres_1917.jpg/255px-Australian_infantry_small_box_respirators_Ypres_1917.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Australian_infantry_small_box_respirators_Ypres_1917.jpg/340px-Australian_infantry_small_box_respirators_Ypres_1917.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Australian_infantry_small_box_respirators_Ypres_1917.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Soldiers of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Australian_4th_Division" title="Australian 4th Division">Australian 4th Division</a> equipped for <a href="/wiki/Chemical_weapons_in_World_War_I" title="Chemical weapons in World War I">chemical warfare in WWI</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Third_Battle_of_Ypres" title="Third Battle of Ypres">Ypres sector</a>, 1917</div></div></div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Asymmetric_warfare" title="Asymmetric warfare">Asymmetric warfare</a> is a conflict between <a href="/wiki/Belligerent" title="Belligerent">belligerents</a> of drastically different levels of military capability or size.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Biological_warfare" title="Biological warfare">Biological warfare</a>, or germ warfare, is the use of weaponized biological toxins or infectious agents such as bacteria, viruses, and fungi.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chemical_warfare" title="Chemical warfare">Chemical warfare</a> involves the use of weaponized chemicals in combat. Poison gas as a <a href="/wiki/Chemical_warfare" title="Chemical warfare">chemical weapon</a> was principally used during <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, and resulted in over a million estimated casualties, including more than 100,000 civilians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cold_warfare" title="Cold warfare">Cold warfare</a> is an intense international rivalry without direct military conflict, but with a sustained threat of it, including high levels of military preparations, expenditures, and development, and may involve active conflicts by indirect means, such as <a href="/wiki/Economic_warfare" title="Economic warfare">economic warfare</a>, <a href="/wiki/Political_warfare" title="Political warfare">political warfare</a>, <a href="/wiki/Covert_operation" title="Covert operation">covert operations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Espionage" title="Espionage">espionage</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cyberwarfare" title="Cyberwarfare">cyberwarfare</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Proxy_war" title="Proxy war">proxy wars</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Conventional_warfare" title="Conventional warfare">Conventional warfare</a> is declared war between states in which <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapon" title="Nuclear weapon">nuclear</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biological_weapon" title="Biological weapon">biological</a>, or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chemical_weapons" title="Chemical weapons">chemical weapons</a> are not used or see limited deployment.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cyberwarfare" title="Cyberwarfare">Cyberwarfare</a> involves the actions by a nation-state or international organization to attack and attempt to damage another nation's information systems.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Insurgency" title="Insurgency">Insurgency</a> is a rebellion against authority, when those taking part in the rebellion are not recognized as belligerents (lawful combatants). An insurgency can be fought via <a href="/wiki/Counterinsurgency" title="Counterinsurgency">counterinsurgency</a>, and may also be opposed by measures to protect the population, and by political and economic actions of various kinds aimed at undermining the insurgents' claims against the incumbent regime.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Information_warfare" title="Information warfare">Information warfare</a> is the application of destructive force on a large scale against information assets and systems, against the <a href="/wiki/Computer" title="Computer">computers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Computer_network" title="Computer network">networks</a> that support the four critical infrastructures (the power grid, communications, financial, and transportation).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nuclear_warfare" title="Nuclear warfare">Nuclear warfare</a> is warfare in which <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapon" title="Nuclear weapon">nuclear weapons</a> are the primary, or a major, method of achieving capitulation.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Total_war" title="Total war">Total war</a> is warfare by any means possible, disregarding the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Laws_of_war" title="Laws of war">laws of war</a>, placing no limits on <a href="/wiki/Legitimate_military_target" title="Legitimate military target">legitimate military targets</a>, using <a href="/wiki/Weapon" title="Weapon">weapons</a> and <a href="/wiki/Military_tactics" title="Military tactics">tactics</a> resulting in significant <a href="/wiki/Civilian_casualties" title="Civilian casualties">civilian casualties</a>, or demanding a <a href="/wiki/War_effort" title="War effort">war effort</a> requiring significant sacrifices by the friendly civilian population.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Unconventional_warfare" title="Unconventional warfare">Unconventional warfare</a>, the opposite of conventional warfare, is an attempt to achieve military victory through acquiescence, capitulation, or clandestine support for one side of an existing conflict.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Aims">Aims</span></h2>
<p>Entities contemplating going to war and entities considering whether to end a war may formulate <i>war aims</i> as an evaluation/propaganda tool. War aims may stand as a proxy for national-military resolve.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Definition">Definition</span></h3>
<p>Fried defines war aims as "the desired territorial, economic, military or other benefits expected following successful conclusion of a war".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Classification">Classification</span></h3>
<p>Tangible/intangible aims:
</p>
<ul><li>Tangible war aims may involve (for example) the acquisition of territory (as in the German goal of <a href="/wiki/Lebensraum" title="Lebensraum">Lebensraum</a> in the first half of the 20th century) or the recognition of economic concessions (as in the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Dutch_Wars" title="Anglo-Dutch Wars">Anglo-Dutch Wars</a>).</li>
<li>Intangible war aims â like the accumulation of credibility or reputation<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup> â may have more tangible expression ("conquest restores prestige, annexation increases power").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Explicit/implicit aims:
</p>
<ul><li>Explicit war aims may involve published policy decisions.</li>
<li>Implicit war aims<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup> can take the form of minutes of discussion, memoranda and instructions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Positive/negative aims:
</p>
<ul><li>"Positive war aims" cover tangible outcomes.</li>
<li>"Negative war aims" forestall or prevent undesired outcomes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>War aims can change in the course of conflict and may eventually morph into "peace conditions"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup> â the minimal conditions under which a state may cease to wage a particular war.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Effects">Effects</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wars-Long-Run-military-civilian-fatalities.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2133" data-file-width="3264" decoding="async" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Wars-Long-Run-military-civilian-fatalities.png/220px-Wars-Long-Run-military-civilian-fatalities.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Wars-Long-Run-military-civilian-fatalities.png/330px-Wars-Long-Run-military-civilian-fatalities.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Wars-Long-Run-military-civilian-fatalities.png/440px-Wars-Long-Run-military-civilian-fatalities.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wars-Long-Run-military-civilian-fatalities.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Global deaths in conflicts since the year 1400.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup></div></div></div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_war" title="Effects of war">Effects of war</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military_and_civilian_casualties_in_recent_human_history">Military and civilian casualties in recent human history</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:War_world_map_-_DALY_-_WHO2004.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="415" data-file-width="940" decoding="async" height="97" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/War_world_map_-_DALY_-_WHO2004.svg/220px-War_world_map_-_DALY_-_WHO2004.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/War_world_map_-_DALY_-_WHO2004.svg/330px-War_world_map_-_DALY_-_WHO2004.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/War_world_map_-_DALY_-_WHO2004.svg/440px-War_world_map_-_DALY_-_WHO2004.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:War_world_map_-_DALY_-_WHO2004.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Disability-adjusted_life_year" title="Disability-adjusted life year">Disability-adjusted life year</a> for war per 100,000Â inhabitants in 2004<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[36]</a></sup><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1054258005">.mw-parser-output .refbegin{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .refbegin-hanging-indents>ul{margin-left:0}.mw-parser-output .refbegin-hanging-indents>ul>li{margin-left:0;padding-left:3.2em;text-indent:-3.2em}.mw-parser-output .refbegin-hanging-indents ul,.mw-parser-output .refbegin-hanging-indents ul li{list-style:none}@media(max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .refbegin-hanging-indents>ul>li{padding-left:1.6em;text-indent:-1.6em}}.mw-parser-output .refbegin-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .refbegin-columns ul{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .refbegin-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}</style><div class="refbegin refbegin-columns references-column-count references-column-count-2" style="column-count: 2;"> <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px style="background-color:#ffff65; color:black;">Â </span>Â less than 100</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#fff200; color:black;">Â </span>Â 100â200</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ffdc00; color:black;">Â </span>Â 200â600</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ffc600; color:black;">Â </span>Â 600â1000</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ffb000; color:black;">Â </span>Â 1000â1400</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ff9a00; color:black;">Â </span>Â 1400â1800</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ff8400; color:black;">Â </span>Â 1800â2200</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ff6e00; color:black;">Â </span>Â 2200â2600</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ff5800; color:black;">Â </span>Â 2600â3000</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ff4200; color:black;">Â </span>Â 3000â8000</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ff2c00; color:black;">Â </span>Â 8000â8800</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#cb0000; color:white;">Â </span>Â more than 8800</div> </div></div></div></div>
<p>Throughout the course of human history, the average number of people dying from war has fluctuated relatively little, being about 1 to 10 people dying per 100,000. However, major wars over shorter periods have resulted in much higher casualty rates, with 100-200 casualties per 100,000 over a few years. While conventional wisdom holds that casualties have increased in recent times due to technological improvements in warfare, this is not generally true. For instance, the <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years' War">Thirty Years' War</a> (1618â1648) had about the same number of casualties per capita as <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, although it was higher during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> (WWII). That said, overall the number of casualties from war has not significantly increased in recent times. Quite to the contrary, on a global scale the time since WWII has been unusually peaceful.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_by_death_toll">Largest by death toll</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/List_of_wars_by_death_toll" title="List of wars by death toll">List of wars by death toll</a>, <a href="/wiki/Outline_of_war#Wars" title="Outline of war">Outline of war Â§Â Wars</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Casualty_recording" title="Casualty recording">Casualty recording</a></div>
<p>The deadliest war in history, in terms of the cumulative number of deaths since its start, is <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, from 1939 to 1945, with 60â85Â million deaths, followed by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mongol_conquests" title="Mongol conquests">Mongol conquests</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup> at up to 60Â million. As concerns a belligerent's losses in proportion to its prewar population, the most destructive war in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Modern_history" title="Modern history">modern history</a> may have been the <a href="/wiki/Paraguayan_War" title="Paraguayan War">Paraguayan War</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Paraguayan_War_casualties" title="Paraguayan War casualties">Paraguayan War casualties</a>). In 2013 war resulted in 31,000 deaths, down from 72,000 deaths in 1990.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GDB2013_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-GDB2013-40">[39]</a></sup> In 2003, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Smalley" title="Richard Smalley">Richard Smalley</a> identified war as the sixth biggest problem (of ten) facing humanity for the next fifty years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup> War usually results in significant deterioration of infrastructure and the ecosystem, a decrease in social spending, <a href="/wiki/Famine" title="Famine">famine</a>, large-scale emigration from the war zone, and often the mistreatment of <a href="/wiki/Prisoner_of_war" title="Prisoner of war">prisoners of war</a> or civilians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup> For instance, of the nine million people who were on the territory of the <a href="/wiki/Byelorussian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Byelorussian Soviet Socialist Republic">Byelorussian SSR</a> in 1941, some 1.6Â million were killed by the Germans in actions away from battlefields, including about 700,000 prisoners of war, 500,000 Jews, and 320,000 people counted as partisans (the vast majority of whom were unarmed civilians).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup> Another byproduct of some wars is the prevalence of <a href="/wiki/Propaganda" title="Propaganda">propaganda</a> by some or all parties in the conflict,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup> and increased revenues by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weapons_manufacturers" title="Weapons manufacturers">weapons manufacturers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup>
</p><p>Three of the ten most costly wars, in terms of loss of life, have been waged in the last century. These are the two World Wars, followed by the <a href="/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War" title="Second Sino-Japanese War">Second Sino-Japanese War</a> (which is sometimes considered part of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, or as overlapping). Most of the others involved China or neighboring peoples. The death toll of World War II, being over 60Â million, surpasses all other war-death-tolls.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-users.erols_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-users.erols-48">[47]</a></sup>
</p>
